It is a multiplicative factor, and\\n2905:     so a dimensionless quantity.\\n2906: \\n2907:     It is defined as the exponential of the standard deviation of the\\n2908:     natural logarithms of the observations.\\n2909: \\n2910:     Parameters\\n2911:     ----------\\n2912:     a : array_like\\n2913:         An array containing finite, strictly positive, real numbers.\\n2914: \\n2915:         .. deprecated:: 1.14.0\\n2916:             Support for masked array input was deprecated in\\n2917:             SciPy 1.14.0 and will be removed in version 1.16.0.\\n2918: \\n2919:     axis : int, tuple or None, optional\\n2920:         Axis along which to operate. Note that the default ``ddof=1`` is different from\\n2951:     the default value used by similar functions, such as `numpy.std` and `numpy.var`.\\n2952: \\n2953:     When an observation is infinite, the geometric standard deviation is\\n2954:     NaN (undefined). Non-positive observations will also produce NaNs in the\\n2955:     output because the *natural* logarithm (as opposed to the *complex*\\n2956:     logarithm) is defined and finite only for positive reals.\\n2957:     The geometric standard deviation is sometimes confused with the exponential\\n2958:     of the standard deviation, ``exp(std(a))``. It is a measure of the dispersion\\n3029:     similar to standard deviation or variance, but is much more robust\\n3030:     against outliers [2]_.\\n3031: \\n3032:     The ``rng`` parameter allows this function to compute other\\n3033:     percentile ranges than the actual IQR.
